<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Terminology of the British Isles</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_location.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/British_Isles_location.svg/300px-British_Isles_location.svg.png" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/British_Isles_location.svg/450px-British_Isles_location.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/British_Isles_location.svg/600px-British_Isles_location.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1255" data-file-height="1255" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_location.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #218439; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">The British Isles</a></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg/300px-British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg.png" width="300" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg/450px-British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg/600px-British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_Euler_diagram_15.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Euler_diagram" title="Euler diagram">Euler diagram</a> with an overview of the terminology <br /> <span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b1d79b; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<i>Geographical feature</i>&#160;&#160; <span class="nowrap"><span style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aac2ed; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Legal distinction </span></div></div></div>
<p>The <b>terminology of the British Isles</b> refers to the various words and phrases that are used to describe the different (and sometimes overlapping) geographical and political areas of the islands of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, and the smaller islands which surround them. The terminology is often a source of confusion, partly owing to the similarity between some of the actual words used, but also because they are often used loosely. In addition, many of the words carry both geographical and political connotations which are affected by the history of the islands. 
</p><p>The purpose of this article is to explain the meanings of and relationships among the terms in use; however many of these classifications are contentious and are the subject of disagreement <span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">(See the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles_naming_dispute" title="British Isles naming dispute">British Isles naming dispute</a>)</span>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The use of terminology depends on context; words and phrases can generally be grouped into four main areas: geographical, political, linguistic and sporting terms. In brief, the main terms and their simple explanations are as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>Geographical terms:
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> is a group of islands in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>. It includes <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">thousands of smaller islands</a>. Traditionally the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> are included, though these specific islands are geographically closer to mainland continental Europe, being positioned off the French coast of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>. This, in part, has resulted in the term being <a href="/wiki/British_Isles_naming_dispute" title="British Isles naming dispute">disputed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Written_Answers_-_Official_Terms_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Written_Answers_-_Official_Terms-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a></b> is the largest island of the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a></b> is the second largest island of the archipelago and lies directly to the west of Great Britain. The island of Ireland itself has its own <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Ireland" title="List of islands of Ireland">list of Irish Isles</a></b>.</li>
<li>The full <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">list of islands of the British Isles</a></b> includes over 6,000 islands,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> of which 51 have an area larger than 20&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (7.7&#160;sq&#160;mi).</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li>Political terms:
<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a></b> is the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> occupying the island of Great Britain, the small nearby islands (but not the Isle of Man or the Channel Islands), and the north-eastern part of the island of Ireland. Usually, it is shortened to <i>United Kingdom</i> or <i>the UK</i>, though <i>Britain</i><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> is also an officially recognised short form.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGN-uk-guide_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGN-uk-guide-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> "Great Britain" is sometimes used as a short form, and is the name used by the UK in some international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The abbreviation <i>GB</i> is frequently used for the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland in international agreements, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">Universal Postal Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_on_Road_Traffic" title="Vienna Convention on Road Traffic">Road Traffic Convention</a>, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166</a> country codes (GB and GBR). "England" was also formerly used <a href="/wiki/Synecdoche" title="Synecdoche">synecdochically</a> to refer to the whole United Kingdom, but this usage became rare early in the 20th century.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a></b> is the sovereign republic occupying the larger portion of the island of Ireland. However, to distinguish the state from the island, or to distinguish either of these from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, it is also called "the Republic of Ireland" or simply "the Republic". Occasionally, its <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish-language</a> name, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="Éire">Éire</a></i> (or <i>Eire</i> without the diacritic), will be used in an English-language context to distinguish it from "Northern Ireland", even though the word <i>Éire</i> directly translates as "Ireland".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> are the four <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">countries of the United Kingdom</a>, though they are also referred to, especially in sporting contexts, as the <a href="/wiki/Home_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Home nations">home nations</a> of the United Kingdom.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, Scotland, and Northern Ireland are legal jurisdictions within the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-walesjurisdiction_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walesjurisdiction-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain#Political_definition" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> means the countries of England, Wales and Scotland considered as a unit.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/British_Islands" title="British Islands">British Islands</a> consists of the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>. These are the <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">polities</a> within the British Isles that have the <a href="/wiki/British_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarch">British monarch</a> as head of state.</li></ul></li>
<li>Linguistic terms:
<ul><li>The two <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign states">sovereign states</a> in the region, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, are frequently referred to as <i>countries</i>. So too are <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and, to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> (as is the whole <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Island of Ireland">island of Ireland</a>).</li>
<li>British is an adjective pertaining to the United Kingdom; for example, a <a href="/wiki/Citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizen">citizen</a> of the UK is called a <a href="/wiki/British_citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="British citizen">British citizen</a>—but for citizenship purposes "British" includes the Channel Islands and the Isle of Man.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anglo-" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-">Anglo-</a> is often used as an adjectival prefix referring to the United Kingdom (notwithstanding that its original meaning is "English") particularly in the field of diplomatic relations.  It can also refer to the English language, to anglophone peoples and can have a variety of other shades of meaning.</li>
<li>Wales is sometimes called the <i><a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Wales" title="Principality of Wales">Principality of Wales</a></i>, although this has no modern constitutional basis.</li>
<li>Northern Ireland is often referred to as a <i>province</i> or called <i>Ulster</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ireland" title="Provinces of Ireland">traditional Irish province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> within which it is located.</li></ul></li>
<li>Sport
<ul><li>Forms of national representation vary from sport to sport. England, Scotland and Wales often compete separately as <i>nations</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-worldpeoples_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldpeoples-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In some sports—such as <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>—the island of Ireland competes as a nation; in others, most notably <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, Northern Ireland and the Republic of Ireland field separate teams. In these contexts England, Scotland, Wales and Ireland/Northern Ireland  are sometimes described as <i>the <a href="/wiki/Home_nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Home nations">home nations</a></i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> players from both Ireland and Great Britain play for <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British and Irish Lions</a> representing the four "Home Unions" of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Irish Rugby Football Union">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Rugby_Union" title="Scottish Rugby Union">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Rugby_Union" title="Welsh Rugby Union">Wales</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> is sometimes used to mean <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.  For example, at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, the team called "Great Britain" represents Great Britain and Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Irishand_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irishand-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  However, athletes from Northern Ireland have, by virtue of their entitlement to dual nationality, the choice of participating in either the Great Britain team or the Republic of Ireland team.<sup id="cite_ref-Irishand_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irishand-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the majority of individual sports (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>), at international level competitors are identified as GB if they are from Great Britain or Northern Ireland. A small number of sports (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darts" title="Darts">darts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a>) identify participants as representing their constituent country. In the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>, England, Northern Ireland, Scotland and Wales each compete as separate nations, as do each of the three Crown Dependencies (Ireland is not part of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> and is not eligible to participate).</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_guide">Visual guide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Visual guide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology_in_detail">Terminology in detail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Terminology in detail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Britain_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain (name)">Britain</a></b> is a political and geographic term which can refer to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-num10_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-num10-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> or the island of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a></b> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">largest island</a> in Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">political union</a> of three nations, these being:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a></b> is a political and administrative term referring to the two <a href="/wiki/Home_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Home countries">home countries</a> of England and Wales, which share the same legal system.  Between <a href="/wiki/Wales_and_Berwick_Act_1746" title="Wales and Berwick Act 1746">1746</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Language_Act_1967" title="Welsh Language Act 1967">1967</a> the term "England" did legally include Wales.</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a></b> (see also the historical <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a>).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a></b> (see also the historical <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Wales" title="Principality of Wales">Principality of Wales</a>).</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a></b> (see also the historical <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a>)</li></ul></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<dl><dd><ul><li>The historical <b><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a></b> is Britain for the period 1707–1801.</li>
<li><b>Britannia</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman province of Britain</a>, or a poetic reference to later Britain, or a <a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">personification of Britain</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a></b>, usually shortened to the <b>United Kingdom</b> (abbreviation <b>UK</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-PCGN-uk-guide_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGN-uk-guide-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> comprising <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain#Political_definition" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> plus <b>Northern Ireland</b> since 1927. (The Partition of Ireland took place in 1922, but the consequent change in the official title of the UK was only made by Act of Parliament five years later.) The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a> is often shortened to  <b>Britain</b>, even on official websites,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> where such use is described as "informal".<sup id="cite_ref-dgov-keyfacts_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgov-keyfacts-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-num10_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-num10-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A proposal to rename the political entity as the "<a href="/wiki/Alternative_names_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Alternative names for Northern Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ulster</a>" was formally recommended by civil servants to the Cabinet in 1949 but ultimately rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>The historical <b><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a></b> was <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain#Political_definition" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> plus <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, for the period 1801 to 1922, although the name change after the secession of the Irish Free State only took place in 1927.</li></ul></dd>
<dd>N.B.: While "United Kingdom" is normally abbreviated <b>UK</b>, the official <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166</a> two-letter country code is <b>GB</b> and the three letter code is <b>GBR</b> (<a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> has the two letter code UA and the three letter code UKR). Due to a pre-existing convention originating in the UK's <a href="/wiki/JANET" title="JANET">JANET</a> academic computer network,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> the UK's <a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet top-level domain</a> is <b><a href="/wiki/.uk" title=".uk">.uk</a></b>, a break from the <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a> practice of following ISO 3166 (a <b><a href="/wiki/.gb" title=".gb">.gb</a></b> domain has also been used to a limited extent in the past but is now defunct). <b>GB</b> is also used on car number plates to indicate the United Kingdom.</dd></dl>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a></b>  (in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <i><b>Éire</b></i>) refers, geographically, to the island of Ireland, or to any of the following:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><i>Historically:</i>
<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a></b>  was Ireland for the period 1541–1801. (The <a href="/wiki/King_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Ireland">King of Ireland</a> remained Head of State in the Irish Free State and Ireland/Éire until the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a> abolished that status).</li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a></b>, established by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Irish Declaration of Independence">Irish Declaration of Independence</a>, was a 32-county republic encompassing the entire island, during the period 1919–22—though its <i>de facto</i> rule did not encompass all of the island. During this period, according to British law, Ireland remained part of the UK though its independence was recognised by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Southern_Ireland_(1921%E2%80%9322)" title="Southern Ireland (1921–22)">Southern Ireland</a></b> was a  proposed <a href="/wiki/Home_Rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Rule">Home Rule</a> 26-county state under the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland_Act_1920" title="Government of Ireland Act 1920">Government of Ireland Act 1920</a>. It never came into practical existence, being superseded by:</li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a></b> is Ireland excepting Northern Ireland during the period 1922–37.</li></ul></dd>
<dd><i>Present</i>:
<ul><li><b>Ireland</b> (in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="Éire">Éire</a></i>) is the political entity consisting of the island of Ireland excepting Northern Ireland, 1937–present. This is the name of the state according to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Irish Constitution</a> and the United Nations.</li>
<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a></b> is a commonly used description of Ireland excepting Northern Ireland, 1949–present. It is also the name used by the international <a href="/wiki/Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Football">Association Football</a> team.</li></ul>
<dl><dd>The terms <i>Irish Republic</i>, <i>Southern Ireland</i>, the <i>Irish Free State</i>, the <i>Free State</i>, the <i>26 Counties</i> and <i>Éire</i> (in English-language texts) have been used synonymously with the <i>Republic of Ireland</i>. Of these, <i>Southern Ireland</i> and <i>Irish Free State</i>, in particular, are seen as outdated. "Eire" (spelt without the Irish <i><a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">fada</a></i>) was the British legal spelling from the <a href="/wiki/Eire_(Confirmation_of_Agreements)_Act_1938" title="Eire (Confirmation of Agreements) Act 1938">Eire (Confirmation of Agreements) Act 1938</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Ireland_Act_1949" title="Ireland Act 1949">Ireland Act 1949</a>, and informally for some years after.</dd></dl>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a></b> 1922–present. That part of the island of Ireland northeast of the line of partition of 1922, and which is still part of the United Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/Alternative_names_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Alternative names for Northern Ireland">Various alternative names</a> have been used or proposed for Northern Ireland. It is sometimes referred to as "the North of Ireland", "the Six Counties" or (in extremist usage) the "occupied six counties", especially by <a href="/wiki/Irish_Nationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Nationalism">Irish Nationalists</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a></b>. The name of one of Ireland's four traditional <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ireland" title="Provinces of Ireland">provinces</a>. The area contains nine northern counties, six of which make up <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, and three of which are part of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. It is also often used by <a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_Ireland" title="Unionism in Ireland">Unionists</a> to refer to the smaller <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. Though <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> has not been a political entity since the ancient Gaelic provincial kingdoms, it remains associated with a geographical area and is used in sporting and cultural contexts. See <a href="/wiki/Ulster_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Ulster (disambiguation)">Ulster (disambiguation)</a>.</li></ul></dd>
<dd><i>In sport</i>
<ul><li>In <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_games" title="Gaelic games">Gaelic games</a>, no distinction is recognised between the <a href="/wiki/GAA_county" class="mw-redirect" title="GAA county">GAA counties</a> of the Republic and those of Northern Ireland. County teams play in their provincial championships (where the six counties of Ulster within Northern Ireland and three within the Republic all play in the Ulster championship) and the winners of these play in the All-Ireland championship. Even within Northern Ireland, a tricolour, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Ireland" title="Flag of Ireland">flag of the Republic of Ireland</a>, is flown at all games. At bigger games, where an anthem is played, it is always <a href="/wiki/Amhr%C3%A1n_na_bhFiann" title="Amhrán na bhFiann">the national anthem of the Republic</a>. In the case of the <a href="/wiki/International_rules_football" title="International rules football">International Rules</a> series against <a href="/wiki/Australia_international_rules_football_team" title="Australia international rules football team">Australia</a>, an Irish national team is chosen from all 32 counties.</li>
<li>In Association Football, the teams correspond to political entities: Northern Ireland and the Republic of Ireland. In accordance with <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>'s rules, each of these countries has its own football league: the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Football League">Irish League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Ireland" title="League of Ireland">League of Ireland</a> respectively.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a> and others  the <i>Ireland</i> team is drawn from the whole island (i.e. both the Republic and Northern Ireland). Many sports organisations are subdivided along provincial lines e.g. <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>The <b><a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a></b> is a term used to mean the island of Great Britain plus the island of Ireland and many smaller surrounding islands, including the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and, in some contexts, the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>). See <a href="/wiki/British_Isles_naming_dispute" title="British Isles naming dispute">British Isles naming dispute</a> for details of the conflict over use of this term.</li>
<li><i>Great Britain and Ireland</i>, or variants like "Britain and Ireland" or "The UK and Ireland" are sometimes used as alternatives to the term <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>.</li>
<li><b>Anglo-Celtic Isles</b> is an alternative term (in limited use) for the geographic region comprising Britain &amp; Ireland, more commonly referred to as the 'British Isles'. 'Anglo-Celtic Islands' is a derivative of this. It is intended as a geographic term free of any political implication and uses the macro-cultural grouping term <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic" title="Anglo-Celtic">Anglo-Celtic</a>, referring to the peoples from which the majority of the island group's population are descended—the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celts</a> (it can also be inclusive of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Normans" title="Anglo-Normans">Anglo-Normans</a>).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Islands_of_the_North_Atlantic" title="Islands of the North Atlantic">Islands of the North Atlantic</a></b> is another suggested replacement term for 'British Isles', without the same political connotations. However, its convolution and impracticality due to implying inclusion of fellow North Atlantic islands such as Iceland have made it unworkable and it has not come into common use. The term was used as part of the Strand 3 level of negotiations for the Belfast agreement. (Its acronym, IONA, is also the name of the small but historically important island of <a href="/wiki/Iona" title="Iona">Iona</a> off the coast of Scotland.)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/British_Islands" title="British Islands">British Islands</a></b> (a legal term not in common usage) is the UK, the Isle of Man, and the Channel Islands.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a></b>, itself a corruption of 'Britain', and sometimes formerly known as 'Little Britain' is a historical <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">Duchy</a> in the West of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, now a French region; for this modern administrative sense, see <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">Brittany (administrative region)</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_distinctions">Geographical distinctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geographical distinctions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_British_Isles">The British Isles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The British Isles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_all.svg" class="image"><img alt="British Isles all.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/British_Isles_all.svg/50px-British_Isles_all.svg.png" width="50" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/British_Isles_all.svg/75px-British_Isles_all.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/British_Isles_all.svg/100px-British_Isles_all.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
</td>
<td>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> is a group of islands in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>. It includes <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">thousands of smaller islands</a>. Traditionally the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>, are included, however these specific islands are geographically part of mainland continental Europe, as they are positioned off the French coast of Normandy. The term is disputed (see <a href="/wiki/British_Isles_naming_dispute" title="British Isles naming dispute">British Isles naming dispute</a>).
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Britain">Great Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Great Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Britain.svg" class="image"><img alt="Great Britain.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Great_Britain.svg/50px-Great_Britain.svg.png" width="50" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Great_Britain.svg/75px-Great_Britain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Great_Britain.svg/100px-Great_Britain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> is the largest of the British Isles. On Great Britain are located three constituent countries of the United Kingdom: <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> in the south and east and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> in the west. There are also <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">numerous smaller islands</a> off its coast (<i>not</i> coloured red on the attached map) that are administered as part of England, Scotland and Wales.  The inclusion of these smaller islands means political 'Great Britain' covers a slightly larger area than the island of Great Britain.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:Island_of_Ireland.svg" class="image"><img alt="Island of Ireland.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Island_of_Ireland.svg/50px-Island_of_Ireland.svg.png" width="50" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Island_of_Ireland.svg/75px-Island_of_Ireland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Island_of_Ireland.svg/100px-Island_of_Ireland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
</td>
<td>The second largest island in the group is <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. Most of the island is in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. The north east of the island (<a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>) is part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. There are also <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Ireland" title="List of islands of Ireland">numerous smaller islands</a> off the coast of Ireland.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Isle_of_Man">Isle of Man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Isle of Man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg" class="image"><img alt="British Isles Isle of Man.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg/50px-British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg.png" width="50" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg/75px-British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg/100px-British_Isles_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
</td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> lies between Great Britain and Ireland. It is governed as a British <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependency" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown dependency">Crown dependency</a>, having its own parliament, but with the United Kingdom responsible for its defence and external relations.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_Islands">Channel Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Channel Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/File:British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg" class="image"><img alt="British Isles Channel Islands.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg/50px-British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg.png" width="50" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg/75px-British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg/100px-British_Isles_Channel_Islands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a>
</td>
<td>Although the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> are associated with the United Kingdom politically as <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>, they are geographically an outcrop of the nearby French mainland (specifically, the <a href="/wiki/Armorican_massif" class="mw-redirect" title="Armorican massif">Armorican massif</a>), and historically they are the last remaining parts of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Duchy of Normandy</a>, the Duke of Normandy being a title belonging to the British monarch.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_terms_in_more_detail">Political terms in more detail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Political terms in more detail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_United_Kingdom">The United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg" class="image"><img alt="United Kingdom in the British Isles.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg/80px-United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg.png" width="80" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg/120px-United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg/160px-United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_passport_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/British_passport_2002.jpg/130px-British_passport_2002.jpg" width="130" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/British_passport_2002.jpg/195px-British_passport_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/British_passport_2002.jpg/260px-British_passport_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="1366" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_passport_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A UK passport</div></div></div>
<p><i>The United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</i> is the official full title of the state. This name appears on official documentation such as <a href="/wiki/British_passport" title="British passport">British passports</a>. For convenience, the name is usually shortened to <i>United Kingdom</i>, <i>UK</i> or <i>Britain</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGN-uk-guide_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGN-uk-guide-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dgov-keyfacts_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgov-keyfacts-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <b>United Kingdom</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>. Its four <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">constituent countries</a> are sometimes considered to be of different status. This view may be supported by the existence of <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> governments with different levels of power in Scotland, Northern Ireland and Wales (see <a href="/wiki/Asymmetrical_federalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Asymmetrical federalism">Asymmetrical federalism</a>).
</p><p>Wales is also often erroneously<sup id="cite_ref-Wales_FAQ_page_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wales_FAQ_page-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> described as a <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> of the United Kingdom. The title of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> is usually given to the <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> to the <a href="/wiki/British_throne" class="mw-redirect" title="British throne">British throne</a> but it has no political or other role in respect of Wales. The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Organization for Standardisation">International Organization for Standardisation</a> (ISO) has defined Wales as a "country" rather than a "principality" since 2011, following a recommendation by the <a href="/wiki/British_Standards_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="British Standards Institute">British Standards Institute</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Government" title="Welsh Government">Welsh Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> is sometimes described by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> citizens as a <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">province</a> of the United Kingdom, which derives from the Irish <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ireland" title="Provinces of Ireland">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>, of which <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> is a part. Northern Ireland also had, until 1972, a far greater degree of <a href="/wiki/Self-government" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-government">self-government</a> than the other constituent parts of the UK.
</p><p><i>Great Britain</i> is both a geographical and a political entity. Geographically, it is one island, but <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain#Political_definition" title="Great Britain">as a political entity</a> it also includes the smaller offshore islands that are administered as part of its constituent nations – England, Wales and Scotland – such as England's <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>, Wales' <a href="/wiki/Anglesey" title="Anglesey">Anglesey</a> and Scotland's <a href="/wiki/Inner_Hebrides" title="Inner Hebrides">Inner Hebrides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outer_Hebrides" title="Outer Hebrides">Outer Hebrides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Orkney Islands">Orkney Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetland Islands">Shetland Islands</a>.
</p><p>The abbreviation <i>GB</i> is sometimes officially used for the United Kingdom, for example in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympics</a>, or as the <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plate#International_codes" title="Vehicle registration plate">vehicle registration plate</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_international_license_plate_codes" class="mw-redirect" title="List of international license plate codes">country identification code</a> for UK-registered cars <i>(see also <a href="/wiki/British_car_number_plates" class="mw-redirect" title="British car number plates">British car number plates</a>)</i>. <i>SCO</i> in Scotland, <i>CYM</i> for Wales (Cymru), <i>NI</i> for Northern Ireland, or <i>ENG</i> for England can also be used.<sup id="cite_ref-numberplates_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-numberplates-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Internet_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet code">internet code</a> <i><a href="/wiki/.gb" title=".gb">.gb</a>,</i> although allocated to the UK, is virtually unused and UK web domains use <i><a href="/wiki/.uk" title=".uk">.uk</a></i>.
</p><p>The four constituent parts of the UK are also known, particularly in sporting contexts, as <i><a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">Home Nations</a></i> or the "Four Nations". The BBC refers to its UK-wide broadcasting operation as <i>Nations and Regions</i> <sup id="cite_ref-bbcnations_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnations-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> ("regions" referring to geographic regions of England. Thus the UK naming conventions tend towards describing distinct <i>regions</i> or <i>nations</i> which exist within a single sovereign <i>state</i>.
</p><p>In sport, the UK Nations mostly have their own separate national teams – England, Wales, Scotland, Northern Ireland, for example in <a href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Football (soccer)">football</a>. Sporting contests between the Four Nations are known as "Home internationals" (an example is the <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Championship" title="British Home Championship">British Home Championship</a> in football).
</p><p>The governing body for football in Northern Ireland is called the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Football_Association" title="Irish Football Association">Irish Football Association</a> (the IFA), having been in existence since some forty years before <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Ireland" title="Partition of Ireland">Partition</a>. Its counterpart in the Republic (plus <a href="/wiki/Derry_City_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Derry City FC">Derry City FC</a>) is the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Ireland" title="Football Association of Ireland">Football Association of Ireland</a> (the FAI). The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland national team</a> retained the name "Ireland" for some fifty years after partition. Since around 1970 the two teams have been consistently referred to as "Northern Ireland" and "<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>" respectively. The UK competes as Great Britain at the Olympic Games. According to the Olympic Charter the Olympic Council of Ireland represents the entire island of Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-olympicrow_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympicrow-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  Olympic athletes from Northern Ireland may choose whether to represent the UK or the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>.
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> and the subsequent implementation legislation, sporting organisation (and several other organisations, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourism in Ireland">tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Gaelic">Irish Gaelic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a> language boards) on the island of Ireland has increasingly been cross-border.
</p><p>Citizens of the UK are called <i>British</i>, <i>Brits</i>, <i>Britons</i> or <i>Britisher</i> (archaic). The term <i>Unionists</i> may also be used, sometimes <a href="/wiki/Pejoratively" class="mw-redirect" title="Pejoratively">pejoratively</a>, for example by supporters of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a> when referring to supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Union</a>. Some older slang names for Britons are <i>Tommy</i> (for British soldiers) and <i>Anglo</i>. <a href="/wiki/Anglo" title="Anglo">Anglo</a> properly refers only to England, but it is sometimes used as a broader reference as an element in compound adjectives: for example, "Anglo-French relations" may be used in newspaper articles when referring to relations between the political entities <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the United Kingdom. <i>Anglo-Saxon</i> may be used (particularly in Continental European languages) when referring to the whole <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_world" title="English-speaking world">English-speaking world</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland_2">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Irish_state" title="Names of the Irish state">Names of the Irish state</a></div>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:Republic_of_Ireland.svg" class="image"><img alt="Republic of Ireland.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Republic_of_Ireland.svg/80px-Republic_of_Ireland.svg.png" width="80" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Republic_of_Ireland.svg/120px-Republic_of_Ireland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Republic_of_Ireland.svg/160px-Republic_of_Ireland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eirepas.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/130px-Eirepas.JPG" width="130" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/195px-Eirepas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eirepas.JPG/260px-Eirepas.JPG 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="842" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eirepas.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Irish passport</div></div></div>
<p>Since the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a> in 1937, <b><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a></b> has been the <a href="/wiki/English_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="English (language)">English</a> name of the state which covers approximately five-sixths of the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. The name <b><a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="Éire">Éire</a></b> is used when writing in <a href="/wiki/Irish_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish (language)">Irish</a>.
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">Republic of Ireland Act 1948</a>, the term "Republic of Ireland" is the term used as the additional <i>description</i> of the state. This term is useful in avoiding ambiguity between the name of the island and the name of the state.  However, the term "Ireland" is always used in formal diplomatic contexts such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> or the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. The passport of the Republic of Ireland bears the name <i>Éire – Ireland</i>.
</p><p>Before the introduction of the 1937 constitution and the new name, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> occupied the same territory as the modern state of Ireland. The Irish Free State became an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> in 1922 when it seceded from the United Kingdom through the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a>. The King ceased to be its Head of State <a href="/wiki/Executive_Authority_(External_Relations)_Act_1936" title="Executive Authority (External Relations) Act 1936">in 1936</a> and the state ceased to be a Dominion and left the Commonwealth <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_Act_1948" title="Republic of Ireland Act 1948">in 1948</a>.
</p><p>Traditionally, the island of Ireland is divided into four <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Ireland" title="Provinces of Ireland">provinces</a> – <a href="/wiki/Leinster" title="Leinster">Leinster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Connacht" title="Connacht">Connacht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munster" title="Munster">Munster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>, with each of the provinces further divided into counties. The Republic of Ireland takes up 83% of the island, twenty-six of the thirty-two traditional counties of Ireland. Northern Ireland takes up the remaining area, six of the traditional nine counties of Ulster.
</p><p>On the island of Ireland the naming of places often raises political issues. The usage of "Ireland" as the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">official name</a> of the state causes offence to some <a href="/wiki/Unionists_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Unionists (Ireland)">Unionists</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, who believe it implies that the state <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_of_the_Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Nineteenth Amendment of the Constitution of Ireland">still</a> has a territorial claim to the whole island – the terminology of "Republic of Ireland" or "<a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="Éire">Éire</a>" is much preferred by Northern Irish unionists when referring to that political state. Similarly, some <a href="/wiki/Nationalists_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalists (Ireland)">Nationalists</a> in Northern Ireland also prefer to reserve the usage of "Ireland" to refer to the whole island.
</p><p>In Northern Ireland, Irishness is a highly contested identity, with fundamentally different perceptions of national identity between unionists (who generally perceive themselves as being British) and nationalists (who generally consider both communities to be part of the Irish nation).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Republic of Ireland is often referred to by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish nationalists">Nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Republicans">Republican</a> communities by the term "the Twenty-six Counties", with the connotation that the state constituted as such forms only a portion of the ideal political unit of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a>, which would consist of all of the <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">thirty-two counties</a> into which the island is divided.  The term "the Six Counties" (of Northern Ireland) is also used. Other Nationalist terms in use include "the North of Ireland" and "the North". These latter are terms also used by the Irish national broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidió Teilifís Éireann">RTÉ</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  More extreme terms for Northern Ireland include "the occupied six counties" or "occupied Ireland", which are often used by people who reject the idea of Northern Ireland as a separate entity from the Republic of Ireland.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_passport" title="Irish passport">Irish passport</a> is available to Irish citizens and can also be applied for abroad through Irish Consular services and the local Irish Embassy. As per the <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationality_law" title="Irish nationality law">Irish nationality law</a>, any person born on the island of Ireland before 2005, or otherwise a first generation descendant of such a person, is allowed to apply for an Irish passport. As such, people born in Northern Ireland and their children may be Irish citizens and hold an Irish passport if they choose.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Islands">British Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: British Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Islands.svg" class="image"><img alt="British Islands.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/British_Islands.svg/80px-British_Islands.svg.png" width="80" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/British_Islands.svg/120px-British_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/British_Islands.svg/160px-British_Islands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="1180" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_passport_new.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Jersey_passport_new.jpg/130px-Jersey_passport_new.jpg" width="130" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Jersey_passport_new.jpg/195px-Jersey_passport_new.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Jersey_passport_new.jpg/260px-Jersey_passport_new.jpg 2x" data-file-width="527" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_passport_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Jersey passport</div></div></div>
<p>Under the Interpretation Act 1978 of the United Kingdom, the legal term <i><b>British Islands</b></i> (as opposed to the geographical term <i>British Isles</i>) refers to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a>, together with the <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick" title="Bailiwick">Bailiwicks</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a> (which in turn includes the smaller islands of <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herm" title="Herm">Herm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>.
</p><p>Special British passports are issued to citizens of the Crown dependencies. On the front of passports issued to residents of the Crown dependencies, the words <i>"United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland"</i> are replaced with <i>"British Islands"</i> followed by the name of the issuing state or island. This design applies to <a href="/wiki/Jersey_passport" title="Jersey passport">Jersey passport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_passport" title="Guernsey passport">Guernsey passport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_passport" title="Isle of Man passport">Isle of Man passport</a>.  Like UK passports, Crown dependency also bear the title <i>"European Union"</i> for customs purposes. However, Crown dependency citizens who have no family ties to the United Kingdom are granted a special limited "Islander Status" under EU law (article 6 of Protocol 3 in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_1972" title="Treaty of Accession 1972">Treaty of Accession of the UK to the European Community</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_aspects">Historical aspects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Historical aspects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Britain_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain (name)">Britain (name)</a></div>
<p>Some suggest an early known  for the term might be  from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greek</a> writings. Though some of the original texts have been lost, excerpts were quoted or paraphrased by later authors. Parts of the <a href="/wiki/Massaliote_Periplus" title="Massaliote Periplus">Massaliote Periplus</a>, a merchants' handbook describing searoutes of the sixth century BC, were used in translation in the writings of <a href="/wiki/Avienus" title="Avienus">Avienus</a> around AD 400. Ireland was referred to as <i>Ierne</i> (<i>Insula sacra</i>, the <i>sacred island</i>, as the Greeks interpreted it) "inhabited by the race of <i>Hiberni</i>" (<i>gens hiernorum</i>), and Britain as <i>insula Albionum</i>, "island of the <a href="/wiki/Albion" title="Albion">Albions</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Several sources from around 150 BC to AD 70 include fragments of the travel writings of the ancient Greek <a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a> around 320 BC, use the terms <i>Albion</i> and <i>Ierne</i><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ArOntheCosmos_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArOntheCosmos-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and have been described as referring to the British Isles, including Ireland, as the <i>Prettanic</i> or <i>Brettanic Islands</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Βρεττανικαὶ νῆσοι</span>) or as <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">αἱ Βρεττανιαι</span>, literally "the Britains".<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ArOntheCosmos_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArOntheCosmos-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ohi_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
Greek writers called the peoples of these islands the <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Πρεττανοί</span>, later <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Bρεττανοί</span> (alternative spellings of this and of all relative words have a single <a href="/wiki/Tau" title="Tau">tau</a> or a double <a href="/wiki/Nu_(letter)" title="Nu (letter)">nu</a>), a name that possibly corresponds to the <i><a href="/wiki/Priteni" class="mw-redirect" title="Priteni">Priteni</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> These names may have derived from a "<a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic language</a>" term which may have reached Pytheas from the <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gauls</a><sup id="cite_ref-ohi_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> who may have used it as their term for the inhabitants of the islands.
</p><p>The Romans called the inhabitants of Gaul (modern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>) <i>Galli</i> or <i>Celtae</i>, the latter term deriving from the Greek name <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Κελτοί</span> for a central European people.  Antiquarians of the seventeenth century who found language connections developed the idea of a race of <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celts</a> inhabiting the islands, but this term was not used by the Greeks or Romans for the inhabitants of Britain or Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-ece_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ece-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> nor is there any record of the inhabitants of the British Isles referring to themselves as such. Nevertheless, Roman administration later incorporated the province of Britannia into the <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Gaul" title="Praetorian prefecture of Gaul">praetorian prefecture of Gaul</a>, in common with Hispania, which had Celtiberians. <a href="/wiki/Armorica" title="Armorica">Armorica</a>, where the Bretons would settle<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, was part of <i>Gallia Celtica</i>, so there were tertiary relations between the Britons and Gallic Celts at least. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Parisii_(Gaul)" title="Parisii (Gaul)">Parisii</a> of Gallia Celtica are thought to have founded Aldborough in Britain. <a href="/wiki/Belgae" title="Belgae">Belgae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silures" title="Silures">Silures</a> also came from Gallic areas, although not strictly "Celtic", but from <i>Gallia Belgica</i> and <i>Aquitainia</i>.
</p><p><i>Priteni</i> is the source of the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> term <a href="/wiki/Prydain" title="Prydain">Prydain</a>, <i>Britain</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-ohi_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and has the same source as the <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Goidelic</a> term <a href="/wiki/Cruithne_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruithne (people)">Cruithne</a>. The latter referred to the early <a href="/wiki/Brythonic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Brythonic languages">Brythonic</a> speaking inhabitants of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_highlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish highlands">Scottish highlands</a> and the north of Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-ohi_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> who are known as the Cruithne in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, and who the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> called <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Caledonians" title="Caledonians">Caledonians</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romans">Romans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Romans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_britain_400.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Roman_britain_400.jpg/220px-Roman_britain_400.jpg" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Roman_britain_400.jpg/330px-Roman_britain_400.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Roman_britain_400.jpg/440px-Roman_britain_400.jpg 2x" data-file-width="880" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_britain_400.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman Britain in 410</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Caesar%27s_invasions_of_Britain" title="Caesar&#39;s invasions of Britain">Caesar's invasions of Britain</a> brought descriptions of the peoples of what he called <i>Britannia pars interior</i>, "inland Britain", in 55 BC. Throughout Book 4 of his <i>Geography</i>, <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> is consistent in spelling the island Britain (transliterated) as <i>Prettanikē</i>; he uses the terms <i>Prettans</i> or <i>Brettans</i> loosely to refer to the islands as a group – a common generalisation used by classical geographers. For example, in Geography 2.1.18, <i>…οι νοτιώτατοι των Βρεττανών βορειότεροι τούτων εισίν</i> ("…the most southern of the Brettans are further north than this").<sup id="cite_ref-Roseman_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roseman-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He was writing around AD 10, although the earliest surviving copy of his work dates from the 6th century.
<a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> writing around AD 70 uses a Latin version of the same terminology in section 4.102 of his <i><a href="/wiki/Pliny%27s_Natural_History" class="mw-redirect" title="Pliny&#39;s Natural History">Naturalis Historia</a></i>. He writes of Great Britain: <i>Albion ipsi nomen fuit, cum Britanniae vocarentur omnes de quibus mox paulo dicemus.</i> ("Albion was its own name, when all [the islands] were called the Britannias; I will speak of them in a moment"). In the following section, 4.103, Pliny enumerates the islands he considers to make up the Britannias, listing Great Britain, Ireland, and many smaller islands.
In his <i>Geography</i> written in the mid 2nd century and probably describing the position around AD 100,<sup id="cite_ref-ohi_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohi-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> includes both Great Britain (Albion) and Ireland (<a href="/wiki/Hibernia" title="Hibernia">Iwernia</a>) in the so called <i>Bretanic</i> island group. He entitles Book II, Chapter 1 of as <i><a href="/wiki/Hibernia" title="Hibernia">Iwernia</a>, Bretanic Island</i>, and Chapter 2 as <i>Alwion [sic], Bretanic Island</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name <i>Albion</i> for <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> fell from favour, and the island was described in Greek as Πρεττανία or Βρεττανία, in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Britannia</i>, an inhabitant as Βρεττανός, <i>Britannus</i>, with the adjective Βρεττανικός, <i>Britannicus</i>, equating to "British".<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Roman conquest of Britain</a> the name <a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">Britannia</a> was used for the province of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman Britain</a>. The Emperor <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a> was honoured with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_naming_convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman naming convention">agnomen</a> <i>Britannicus</i> as if he were the conqueror, and coins were struck from AD 46 inscribed <small>DE BRITAN, DE BRITANN, DE BRITANNI,</small> or <small>DE BRITANNIS</small>. With the visit of <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> in AD 121 coins introduced a female figure with the label <small>BRITANNIA</small> as a personification or goddess of the place. These and later Roman coins introduced the seated figure of Britannia which would be reintroduced in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the later years of Roman rule Britons who left Latin inscriptions, both at home and elsewhere in the Empire, often described themselves as <i>Brittanus</i> or <i>Britto</i>, and where describing their citizenship gave it as <i>cives</i> of a British tribe or of a <i>patria</i> (homeland) of <i>Britannia</i>, not <i>Roma</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> From the 4th century, many Britons migrated from Roman Britain across the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and founded <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mediaeval_period">Mediaeval period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Terminology_of_the_British_Isles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mediaeval period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britain_802.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Britain_802.jpg/220px-Britain_802.jpg" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Britain_802.jpg/330px-Britain_802.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Britain_802.jpg/440px-Britain_802.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1241" data-file-height="1755" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britain_802.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Britain with part of Ireland in 802</div></div></div>
